‚óŹ Now I have a thorough understanding of everything. Let me lay out what I see
  and the design proposal.

  Here's the picture:

  The current problem: Sets 08, 09, and 10 are internal team meetings processed
  through the main singularity research chain alongside client discovery
  materials (Sets 01-07). This works, but it creates two issues:

  1. Mixed concerns. The main research chain is about understanding the client's
   problem, building toward proposals and deliverables. Team meetings are
  operational ‚ÄĒ action items, assignments, blockers, team dynamics. They're
  fundamentally different in purpose.
  2. Different outputs needed. Client meeting processing optimizes for:
  technical deep dives, business opportunity, people assessment. Team meeting
  processing should optimize for: action items and assignments (who owes what by
   when), blockers and dependencies, decisions made, progress against prior
  action items, team readiness.
  3. As the engagement progresses, team meetings will massively outnumber client
   meetings. You'll have 2-3 team standups per week. If those all get numbered
  into the main chain, the research library becomes hard to navigate ‚ÄĒ you're
  looking for the set about Anupma's database access concerns and wading through
   three standups to find it.

  The proposed design ‚ÄĒ team/ as a mini-singularity:

  cisco/cicd/
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ org_chart.md                    (existing, unchanged)
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ source/                         (client/engagement source materials)
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ research/                       (client/engagement blockchain chain)
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ planning/                       (existing)
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ team/                           (NEW ‚ÄĒ mini-singularity for team
  operations)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ source/                     (raw team meeting transcripts)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ research/                   (blockchain processing of team meetings)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 00_methodology_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 01_standup_people_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 01_standup_action_items_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 01_standup_blockers_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 01_standup_summary_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ 01-02_changes_<date>.md
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ...
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ tracking/                   (living operational docs)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ action_items.md         (cumulative, living)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ blockers.md             (cumulative, living)
  ‚Ēā   ‚Ēā   ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ decisions.md            (cumulative, living)
  ‚Ēā   ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ planning/                   (team-level planning, session handoffs)
  ‚Ēā       ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ session_handoff_<date>.md
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ deliverables/
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ pricing/
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ ...

  Key design decisions I want your input on:

  1. The tracking/ folder. This is the big difference from regular singularity.
  Client research is blockchain-only (never edit old docs). But for team
  operations, you need living documents ‚ÄĒ a cumulative action item tracker that
  gets updated after every meeting, a blockers list that items get removed from
  when resolved. The research chain still captures the immutable record of what
  was said, but tracking/ is the operational view. Think of research as the
  ledger and tracking as the dashboard.
  2. Separate numbering chain. Team meetings get their own 01, 02, 03...
  sequence independent of the main engagement chain. No confusion about "is set
  12 the standup or the Anupma database meeting?"
  3. Different processing focus. Instead of the topic map proposing "technical
  deep dive, business opportunity, speaker dynamics," team meeting processing
  would default to a different set of standard passes:
    - People and dynamics (same as now)
    - Action items and assignments (who, what, when, status of prior items)
    - Blockers, dependencies, and escalations
    - Decisions made and rationale
    - Technical discussion (only if substantive technical content exists)
  4. Source files that are currently in source/ and were processed as sets 08, 
  09, 10. We'd leave the existing research docs where they are (blockchain rule
  ‚ÄĒ never delete). But future team meetings would go in team/source/ and get
  processed in the team/research/ chain.

  Does this match what you're envisioning? And do you want me to go ahead and
  write this up as a session document, or do you want to adjust the structure
  first?

‚óŹ The session document is written at
  claude/2026-04-10_singularity_nested_design/00_exploration_and_design.md.
  Here's a summary of the key design points:

  The dual-track tracking model works like you described: per-meeting action
  items docs in research/ (blockchain, immutable record of "at meeting 03, these
   items were identified and these prior items were reported as done") plus
  living docs in tracking/ (cumulative operational view of where everything
  stands right now). The research chain is the audit trail; tracking is the
  dashboard.

  The cross-reference file (cross_reference.md) is the lookup artifact you asked
   for. It maps team meeting sets to parent chain sets by both set number and by
   topic thread, so you can trace "the GitHub MFA blocker thread appears in Team
   sets 02, 03 and Main sets 09, 10."

  The nested singularity pattern is documented as a general, scalable concept.
  Any sub-singularity follows the same template: source/, research/, documents/,
   planning/, and optionally tracking/, plus a cross_reference.md. The rules
  are: one level of nesting only, parent org chart is the master people
  reference, convergence flows upward (sub-singularity findings enter the parent
   chain as new sets when relevant), and each sub-singularity has its own
  independent numbering chain.

  For the Cisco team-without-Colin meetings, those would be a sibling
  sub-singularity (team_cisco_syncs/) at the same level as team/, with its own
  source/research/documents chain.

  The documents/ folder is included in the template as you requested, for HTML
  reports, formatted status docs, etc.

  The existing sets 08, 09, 10 in the main chain stay put (blockchain rule).
  Future team meetings route to team/. The cross-reference file documents the
  historical overlap.

  Want to review the document and then move on to implementing this in the
  singularity skill, or do you want to adjust the design first?

          -b-singularities (team meetings, project management) need it. R
          -esearch-oriented sub-singularities (vendor evaluation, paralle
          -l discovery tracks) may not.                                  
      321 +7. **The `tracking/` folder is always created.** Even if a sub
          +-singularity does not immediately need living operational docu
          +ments, the folder exists from the start. Tracks that seem pure
          +ly research-oriented at creation time often develop operationa
          +l needs as they mature. Having the folder ready eliminates the
          + decision of "do I need this yet?" and keeps the structure con
          +sistent across all sub-singularities.

  Key changes from Masterminds to BayOne Solutions:

  - No images or external media (Font Awesome icons only)

  The spec also covers the reusable component library (header, footer, cards,
  takeaway bars, definition bars), the gradient progression system for card
  coloring, naming conventions, and how it integrates with singularity's
  existing presentations/ folder convention.

      292 -### Layout 9: Definition Bar + Evolution Row                  
      201 +## Rules for Generating Slides                                
      202  
      294 -**ID:** `evolution-row`                                       
      295 -**When to use:** Showing progression or comparison of 3 approa
          -ches/stages/levels

          -cards                                                         
      203 +1. **No images or external media.** Font Awesome icons only. N
          +o `<img>` tags.                                               
      204 +2. **Self-contained HTML.** Each slide is a complete HTML docu
          +ment with inline `<style>`. CDN links for fonts and icons only
          +.                                                             
      205 +3. **BayOne Solutions branding.** Logo reads "BayOne Solutions
          +." Blue palette throughout.                                   
      206 +4. **Aspect ratio 16:10.** All slides use `aspect-ratio: 16 / 
          +10` on the `.slide` container. Max-width 1100px.              
      207 +5. **Content must fit without scrolling.** If content overflow
          +s, split into multiple slides or reduce text.                 
      208 +6. **No em dashes.** Consistent with singularity deliverable r
          +ules.                                                         
      209 +7. **Professional tone.** No contractions, no emojis, no collo
          +quialisms.                                                    
      210 +8. **Date or context in header-title.** Every content slide sh
          +ows context in the header.                                    
      211 +9. **Mandatory pre-generation reading.** Before generating any
          + presentation slide, the skill (or its agents) must read this 
          +spec AND at least 3 of the example HTML files from `.claude/sk
          +ills/singularity/assets/slide_examples/` to internalize the de
          +sign language. This is enforced by the stop hook.

      338 -## Layout Selection Guide                                     
      339 -                                                              
      340 -| Content Type | Recommended Layout | ID |                    
      341 -|-------------|-------------------|-----|                     
      342 -| Deck opener | Title Slide | `title` |                       
      343 -| Agenda / roadmap | Table of Contents | `agenda` |           
      344 -| Person introduction | Profile | `profile` |                 
      345 -| 3-way overview / comparison | Three-Column Cards | `three-co
          -lumn-cards` |                                                 
      346 -| Deep dive on one topic | Split Panel | `split-concept` |    
      347 -| New concept introduction | Definition Bar + Cards | `definit
          -ion-bar` |                                                    
      348 -| Enumeration (4-6 items) | Grid Cards with Takeaway | `grid-t
          -akeaway` |                                                    
      349 -| Before/after, pros/cons | Two-Column Comparison | `two-colum
          -n-compare` |                                                  
      350 -| Progression / evolution | Evolution Row | `evolution-row` | 
      351 -| Deck closer / Q&A | Closing Slide | `closing` |

      231  
      411 -## Rules for Generating Slides                                
      412 -                                                              
      413 -1. **No images or external media.** Font Awesome icons only. N
          -o `<img>` tags, no image placeholders, no "insert image here" 
          -blocks.                                                       
      414 -2. **Self-contained HTML.** Each slide is a complete HTML docu
          -ment with inline `<style>`. No external CSS files. CDN links f
          -or fonts and icons only.                                      
      415 -3. **BayOne Solutions branding.** Logo reads "BayOne Solutions
          -" (not Masterminds or any other name). Blue palette throughout
          -.                                                             
      416 -4. **Aspect ratio 16:10.** All slides use `aspect-ratio: 16 / 
          -10` on the `.slide` container. Max-width 1100px.              
      417 -5. **Content must fit.** No scrolling. Content must fit within
          - the fixed slide dimensions. If content is too long, split int
          -o multiple slides or reduce text.                             
      418 -6. **Gradient progression for card sequences.** Use the 5-step
          - gradient progression for sequential cards. Consistent across 
          -the deck.                                                     
      419 -7. **Takeaway bars for key insights.** Any slide with multiple
          - cards or a complex argument should end with a takeaway bar su
          -mmarizing the point.                                          
      420 -8. **No em dashes in text.** Consistent with singularity deliv
          -erable rules. Use commas, periods, or "and" instead.          
      421 -9. **Professional tone.** No contractions, no emojis, no collo
          -quialisms. Big Four consulting aesthetic.                     
      422 -10. **Date or context in header-title.** Every content slide s
          -hows either the date or a context label (engagement name, sect
          -ion name) in the header.                                      
      423 -                                                              
      424 ----                                                           
      425 -

      307

      310 +## Flow 7: Create Presentation                                
      311 +                                                              
      312 +**Questions to ask:**                                         
      313 +1. Which engagement? (if not already established)             
      314 +2. What is the presentation for? (client meeting, internal bri
          +efing, status update, executive review)                       
      315 +3. Who is the audience? (technical, executive, mixed)         
      316 +4. What topics should it cover? (or: "pull from the research l
          +ibrary")                                                      
      317 +                                                              
      318 +**Mandatory pre-generation reading (hard gate):**             
      319 +                                                              
      320 +Before writing ANY HTML slide file, the skill MUST read:      
      321 +1. `.claude/skills/singularity/references/presentation_design_
          +language.md` (the design language spec)                       
      322 +2. At least 3 example HTML files from `.claude/skills/singular
          +ity/assets/slide_examples/` to internalize the visual patterns
      323 +                                                              
      324 +This is not optional. The stop hook verifies that presentation
          + files in `presentations/` were generated during a session whe
          +re the design references were read. If generating slides via a
          +gents, each agent's prompt must instruct it to read the spec a
          +nd at least one example before writing.                       
      325 +                                                              
      326 +**Process:**                                                  
      327 +1. Read the design language spec and example slides (mandatory
          +, see above)                                                  
      328 +2. Read prior context from the research library (summaries, re
          +levant detail files)                                          
      329 +3. Propose a slide list with descriptions of what each slide c
          +overs and what layout approach fits the content. These are not
          + rigid template IDs. Describe the layout in plain language (e.
          +g., "dark definition bar introducing the concept, then three c
          +omparison cards below").                                      
      330 +4. Get user approval on the slide list                        
      331 +5. Generate slides. Each slide is a self-contained HTML file f
          +ollowing the BayOne design language.                          
      332 +6. Output to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/
          +<deck_name>_<date>/`                                          
      333 +                                                              
      334 +**Design language principles (not rigid templates):**         
      335 +- The example slides in `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/sli
          +de_examples/` demonstrate patterns that work well, but they ar
          +e a vocabulary, not a grammar                                 
      336 +- Design slides that fit the content. Combine elements from di
          +fferent examples or create new arrangements that follow the de
          +sign language                                                 
      337 +- A well-designed slide that does not match any example exactl
          +y but follows the palette, typography, and component patterns 
          +is better than content forced into an ill-fitting layout      
      338 +                                                              
      339 +**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/pr
          +esentation_design_language.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/as
          +sets/slide_examples/` (read at least 3)                       
      340 +                                                              
      341 +**Rules:**                                                    
      342 +- No images or external media. Font Awesome icons only.       
      343 +- Self-contained HTML per slide. Inline styles. CDN links for 
          +fonts and icons only.                                         
      344 +- BayOne Solutions branding throughout.                       
      345 +- Content must fit without scrolling. Split into multiple slid
          +es if needed.                                                 
      346 +- Same content rules as deliverables: no em dashes, no contrac
          +tions, no emojis, professional tone.                          
      347 +- Offer to run `/big4` on the deck before finalizing.         
      348 +                                                              
      349 +---                                                           
      350 +                                                              
      351  ## Sibling Skills
      352  
      353  | Skill | When to Use | How to Offer |
      354  |-------|------------|--------------|
      314 -| `/big4` | After drafting any deliverable | "Want me to run a
          - quality review on this before finalizing?" |                 
      355 +| `/big4` | After drafting any deliverable or presentation | "
          +Want me to run a quality review on this before finalizing?" | 
      356  | `/pptx-extractor` | User provides .pptx source material | "T
           his is a PowerPoint file. I can use the pptx-extractor to pull
            the content into markdown before processing. Want me to do th

      357  | `/pdf-extractor` | User provides .pdf source material | "Thi

      317 -| Slide skill (TBD) | User needs presentations | Output to `/<

‚óŹ So the pattern Colin is describing doesn't exist yet in the deliverables. He's
   envisioning a capability where:

  1. A diagram is embedded as a thumbnail/preview in the slide or document
  2. There's a button to click that opens the full diagram in a dedicated view
  (new page or overlay)
  3. That dedicated view has a back button to return to the slide

  This would need to be built as a new pattern for the presentation design
  language. Let me think about the right approach.

  Here's my understanding of what you want as a capability added to the skill:

  The Diagram Viewer Pattern:
  - Slides can embed mermaid diagrams as compact previews within the slide
  layout
  - A "View Full Size" button on the diagram opens it in a dedicated
  full-browser view (either a separate HTML file in a charts/ subfolder, or a
  JavaScript-driven full-screen overlay within the same page)
  - The full-size view has a "Back" button that returns to the slide
  - The charts/ subfolder holds the standalone full-size diagram HTML files, one
   per diagram, each self-contained with the mermaid rendering and a back button
  - The slide itself shows a scaled-down version or a styled placeholder with
  the click-to-expand button

  Two implementation approaches:

  1. Separate files (cleaner): The diagram lives in charts/diagram_name.html as
  a full-page mermaid render with a back button (history.back() or link to the
  parent slide). The slide embeds a compact preview and links to it.
  2. In-page overlay (self-contained): JavaScript toggles between the slide view
   and a full-screen diagram overlay within the same HTML file. No separate
  files needed but more complex per-slide.

  I'd lean toward option 1 (separate files in charts/) because it's simpler,
  works with the existing multi-file slide deck pattern, and the chart files are
   reusable across slides or documents. The mermaid theme variables would use
  the blue palette to match the presentation design language.

  Is that what you're envisioning? And should I go ahead and add this as a
  documented capability in the presentation design language spec, create an
  example chart file, and then apply it to slide 02?

‚úĽ Worked for 57s

‚óŹ There it is. A charts/ subfolder with standalone diagram files alongside the

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ This is exactly the pattern. Here's how it works:

  1. In the main document: A .diagram-container holds both the inline mermaid
  rendering AND a .diagram-link that says "Open full-screen diagram" linking to
  charts/filename.html with target="_blank"
  2. In charts/: Standalone full-page HTML files, each with just the title,
  subtitle, the mermaid diagram rendered large, and the mermaid JS. Clean,
  minimal, full-browser view.

  The pattern is simple and elegant:
  <div class="diagram-container">
    <div class="diagram-title">Diagram Title</div>
    <div class="mermaid"><pre class="mermaid-src">...</pre></div>
    <a class="diagram-link" href="charts/diagram_name.html" target="_blank">Open
   full-screen diagram</a>
  </div>

  Now I have everything I need. Let me:
  1. Add this as a documented capability in the presentation design language
  spec
  2. Create the pattern adapted for the slide design language (blue palette
  instead of purple)
  3. Apply it to slide 02 with the build log ecosystem diagram
  4. Create the charts/ subfolder with the standalone diagram file

  Want me to go ahead and do all of that now?

      152 +### Embedded Diagram with Full-Screen Viewer                  
      153 +                                                              
      154 +Mermaid.js diagrams can be embedded in slides with a link to o
          +pen a full-screen version in a new tab. This uses two files: t
          +he slide itself (with a compact inline render) and a standalon
          +e chart file in a `charts/` subfolder.                        
      155 +                                                              
      156 +**In the slide:**                                             
      157 +```html                                                       
      158 +<div class="diagram-container">                               
      159 +  <div class="diagram-title">Diagram Title</div>              
      160 +  <div class="mermaid"><pre class="mermaid-src">graph TB ...</
          +pre></div>                                                    
      161 +  <a class="diagram-link" href="charts/diagram_name.html" targ
          +et="_blank">Open full-screen diagram</a>                      
      162 +</div>                                                        
      163 +```                                                           
      164 +                                                              
      165 +**CSS for the slide:**                                        
      166 +```css                                                        
      167 +.diagram-container {                                          
      168 +  background: var(--bg-subtle, #f8fafc);                      
      169 +  border: 1px solid var(--border);                            
      170 +  border-radius: 12px;

      173 +  overflow: hidden;                                           
      174 +}

         -worked example for items 7-10, similar to how `lam_research/ip_

         -ity methodology.                                               
      44 +These are behavioral rules that emerged from feedback during sl
         +ide generation. Each must be encoded explicitly in the design l
         +anguage spec or the Flow 7 instructions so the skill reproduces
         + this quality on the first pass.                               
      45 +                                                               
      46 +| # | Rule | Feedback Source | Where to Codify |               
      47 +|---|------|----------------|-----------------|                
      48 +| 18 | Bullet formatting (.items/.item) is the DEFAULT for all 
         +card bodies, not paragraphs | "The bullet formatting thing is n
         +eeded on all of them, actually" | design language spec + Flow 7
         + rules |                                                       
      49 +| 19 | Navigation (prev/next/home) is MANDATORY on every slide 
         +in a multi-slide deck | "I think you're missing the JavaScript 
         +buttons from the slides" | design language spec + Flow 7 rules 
         +|                                                              
      50 +| 20 | Content must use SPECIFIC details from source material, 
         +not vague corporate language | "You didn't even talk about the 
         +items as you said. Overall, this is just okay" | Flow 7 rules |
      51 +| 21 | When a section (like access status) has substantive cont
         +ent, give it its own slide | "You did not cover the access stil
         +l needed section well. That should be on its own page" | Flow 7
         + rules |                                                       
      52 +| 22 | Error on more slides rather than dense slides | "I thoug
         +ht you were doing seven... if you need to expand slides into mu
         +ltiple, that's fine by me" | Flow 7 rules |                    
      53 +| 23 | Slide deck proposal must be presented and approved BEFOR
         +E generation | "Does that look right before I generate?" workfl
         +ow worked well | Flow 7 process (already partial) |            
      54 +| 24 | No individual names in content; only on title/closing sl
         +ide presenter credit | Was followed; needs to be explicit | des
         +ign language spec rules |                                      
      55 +| 25 | No direct quotes from any person | "Remember to not put 
         +quotes from people in any of the slides" | design language spec
         + rules |                                                       
      56 +| 26 | Diplomatic framing: problems presented as "alignment nee
         +ded," not as conflicts | "be very diplomatic with phrasing here
         +" | Flow 7 rules |                                             
      57 +| 27 | Architectural ideas framed as preliminary, not finalized
         + plans | "we should not be too forthcoming with ideas and brain
         +storming just yet" | Flow 7 rules |                            
      58 +| 28 | Large diagrams go on their own slide, not crammed into c
         +ontent slides | "Now the other content is not having enough roo
         +m on the page" | design language spec |                        
      59 +| 29 | After every substantive change, maintain a running impro
         +vements tracker in session folder | "I haven't seen you do any 
         +note-taking or edits" | Process rule (meta) |

‚óŹ Now let me give you the organized retrospective. Here's the deep read of where
   we are and where we need to go.

  ---
  Where We Are

  What the singularity skill can do on command today:
  - Process client-facing transcripts/emails into blockchain research chains
  (working since before this session)
  - Generate client deliverables from research (problem restatement, information
   request, preliminary approach, proposals) (working since before this session)
  - NEW: Generate presentations from research (Flow 7 exists, design language
  spec + 7 example slides + stop hook gate) ‚úď

  What we PROVED works by doing the real Srinivas deck:
  - Team transcripts processing through blockchain methodology with
  action-items/blockers/decisions passes
  - Tracking folder dual model (blockchain research + living operational docs)
  - Sub-singularity pattern (cisco/cicd/team/ is the first working instance)
  - Cross-reference file mapping team sets to main chain
  - Embedded mermaid + full-screen chart with back button
  - 8-slide presentation with bullet formatting, navigation, and mermaid diagram
  - Gold-standard quality output

  What the skill CANNOT yet do on command (the gap):
  - The sub-singularity / team / nested pattern is nowhere in SKILL.md or
  reference files. A fresh Claude invocation would not know it exists.
  - The team meeting processing passes (action items, blockers, decisions) are
  not in the document_processing.md reference. A fresh session would use
  client-meeting passes by default.
  - The tracking folder concept isn't documented.
  - The "bullet formatting as default, not paragraph" rule isn't in the spec.
  - The "nav is mandatory" rule isn't in the spec.
  - The "specific details from source, not vague language" rule isn't codified.
  - The "propose slide deck before generating" rule is partial.
  - The gold-standard for presentations doesn't exist in skill assets yet.

  What's Next ‚ÄĒ Prioritized

  Priority 1: Codify the gold standards so the skill has concrete references
  1. Copy the Srinivas deck into .claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_s
  tandards/presentations/srinivas_status/ (8 slides + charts folder, as-is)
  2. Copy cisco/cicd/team/ into
  .claude/skills/singularity/references/worked_example_team/ as a complete
  worked example

  Priority 2: Document the nested singularity pattern in the skill
  3. Create references/nested_singularity.md with the full pattern (structure,
  rules, cross_reference, tracking folder, documents folder)
  4. Create references/team_meeting_processing.md with the
  action-items/blockers/decisions methodology
  5. Add a new section in SKILL.md between Flow 6 and Sibling Skills:
  "Sub-Singularities" with a brief overview that loads the two new references
  when needed
  6. Update references/folder_structure.md to include sub-singularity structure
  and the documents/ folder

  Priority 3: Harden the presentation design language with the lessons learned
  7. Update the design language spec with explicit rules (items 18-28 in the
  tracker): bullets as default, nav mandatory, diagrams on own slide, no
  names/quotes, diplomatic framing
  8. Update Flow 7 in SKILL.md to: read spec + examples + relevant gold
  standard, propose slide list and wait for approval, then generate
  9. Update the stop hook to also verify the gold standards exist, not just the
  examples

  Priority 4: Resolve open questions
  10. Clarify client/ folder with you (separate sub-singularity? alias for
  presentations/?)
  11. Decide: do deliverables get the same "gold standard presentation"
  treatment for the actual completed examples?

  What the Skill Should Be Able to Do After All This

  Given the prompt "I have a meeting with Srinivas tomorrow, here's the
  transcript and a doc from my team, make me a status deck" ‚ÄĒ a fresh session
  should:

  1. Recognize this as presentation work (Flow 7)
  2. Recognize the transcript is a team meeting, not client (routes to team
  sub-singularity)
  3. Process the transcript through team meeting methodology (action items /
  blockers / decisions / tech discussion)
  4. Update tracking docs
  5. Read the design language spec + examples + the Srinivas gold standard
  6. Propose a slide list (with bullets, nav, diagrams on own slides where
  appropriate)
  7. After your approval, generate the deck, all slides with bullets, all slides
   with nav, charts in charts/ subfolder with back buttons
  8. Output quality equal to or better than what we just made, on the first try

  ---
  The single missing piece that would make the biggest difference: the gold
  standard presentation in the skill assets. Right now the skill has example
  slides (one layout each) but no complete deck showing how a real engagement
  presentation comes together. Copying the Srinivas deck into
  gold_standards/presentations/ gives future sessions a concrete target.

  Want me to proceed with Priority 1 (copy the gold standards) and Priority 2
  (document the nested singularity pattern) next? Those two would close the
  biggest gaps.

  I think you did miss one thing, which is that we should have a special carve

  ---
  Open Questions I Had For You

  Q1: client/ folder concept

  You mentioned cisco/cicd/client back when we were first discussing the
  Srinivas deck. Three possible interpretations:

  - A: client/ is a sub-singularity for all client-facing outputs
  (presentations, proposals, status decks delivered to the client). In this
  model, presentations/ at the engagement root would be internal/BayOne-facing
  only.
  - B: client/ is just the presentations folder with a different name because
  "presentations" is too generic.
  - C: client/ is something else entirely ‚ÄĒ maybe a sub-singularity that
  includes client-facing transcripts, meeting notes where client-facing team
  delivered something, AND presentations.

  Which one is it?

  Q2: Gold standard treatment for deliverables

  The Srinivas deck became a gold standard because it was a real end-to-end
  working deck. Should we do the same treatment for:

  - A full problem restatement + information request + preliminary approach set
  as an end-to-end gold standard deliverable chain (each exists today as a
  standalone but not as a chain)?
  - A full formal proposal with pricing?
  - A team status presentation chain (week 1, week 2, week 3 showing how
  tracking docs evolve over time)?

  Q3: Depth of methodology enforcement

  The singularity skill currently uses two kinds of enforcement:
  - Behavioral instructions in SKILL.md (the skill is told what to do)
  - Deterministic hook checks (the skill is verified to have done it)

  Is the current balance right, or should more checks be added? Should any be
  removed if they cause friction?

  Q4: When to offer vs. enforce sub-singularity creation

  Some engagements clearly benefit from a team sub-singularity (operational,
  many standups). Others don't need one. Should the skill:

  - Always offer the option at engagement creation?
  - Only create one when explicitly asked?
  - Detect automatically (e.g., 2+ internal team meetings processed implies one
  should exist)?

  Q5: Cross-engagement learning

  Patterns emerge across engagements ("most of these produce a scraper-type
  task," "most of these hit a GitHub MFA issue"). Is there a case for a
  cross-engagement knowledge layer the skill consults, or is that scope creep?

  Q6: Backup and recovery

  The blockchain chains are append-only. If a file gets accidentally modified or
   deleted, is there a recovery pattern you want? Should there be?

  ---
  Answer any of these you have opinions on, and I'll update the file + to-do
  list accordingly. Some may have obvious answers, others may deserve longer
  discussion. Also ready whenever you want to share your own open questions.

‚úĽ Cooked for 8m 45s

‚ĚĮ Why do we need to do that before phase one? Just explain. I'm not challenging 
   it; I just want to understand.                                               

‚óŹ Phase 0 is rule-codification; Phase 1 is producing gold standards (copying the
   Srinivas deck and team sub-singularity into the skill assets). The reason
  Phase 0 goes first:

  The gold standards will be referenced in future sessions as "this is how good 
  work looks." If the rules aren't codified first, any follow-on work ‚ÄĒ 
  including the act of writing the gold standard README files, or the 
  worked-example README, or the updates to the design language spec ‚ÄĒ is at risk
   of the same failure patterns we just catalogued.

  Concrete example: Phase 1.1 asks me to write a README for the Srinivas deck
  gold standard explaining what each slide demonstrates. That README will be
  read by future sessions as authoritative. If I'm not enforcing "bring
  perspective not just questions," "paraphrase not verbatim," "align on
  structure first," etc. while writing it, the README itself could be low
  quality ‚ÄĒ and then it becomes a bad example that perpetuates the problem.

  Another way to put it: Phase 0 is about Claude's behavior. Phases 1-5 are
  about Claude's outputs. Bad behavior produces bad outputs. Fixing behavior
  first means every subsequent phase benefits.

  A secondary reason: Phase 0 is cheap. It's editing SKILL.md to add a Hard
  Rules section and making sure the rules are loaded every invocation. It
  doesn't require reading example HTML files, writing deliverables, or
  generating slides. If Phase 0 takes an hour, the remaining four phases all
  start from a firmer footing.

  That said ‚ÄĒ if you'd rather start Phase 1 first and do Phase 0 in parallel or
  after, it's not structurally impossible. Phase 1 is mechanical copying plus
  README writing. The risk is that whatever quality issues creep into the Phase
  1 outputs then become "the standard" that Phase 0 is supposed to prevent.

‚ĚĮ Okay, let's do phase zero as you said. One thing to realize is that           
  eventually we are going to have to transfer all of this into the ultimate     
  skill location once we are sure that it works. We should keep tabs on what we 
   are changing and what we are doing.                                          
                                                                                
  To explain, there is another repository which contains the master skill       
  definitions for all skills that we have. I don't want to update that one yet  
  until we know what we changed here, but it would need to know about every     
  single change that we made in reality. We don't need to be exhaustive with    
  that in the full sense, because what we will simply do is tell another Claude 
   session in that repository to look at our version of the singularity skill.  
  Any notes we can take along the way will surely be helpful. We just don't     
  need to do line-level comments or things like that, because the Claude        
  session will already be able to figure out what the differences are versus    
  the existing skill in that master repository. Does that make sense to you?    

‚óŹ Yes, that makes sense.

  To make sure we're aligned:

  - This repo is the working copy where the skill evolves in real use
  - The other repo is the master skill definitions ‚ÄĒ authoritative, only updated
   once changes are proven here
  - When it's time to sync, we point a Claude session at that repo and tell it
  "compare the singularity skill here to the singularity skill at <this path>
  and bring over the changes"
  - That session does the heavy lifting via diff ‚ÄĒ it doesn't need a surgical
  change log from us
  - What WE need is a lightweight summary log of what we changed and why, so the
   receiving session has context to evaluate the changes (not just blindly apply
   them)

  What I'll keep: a running "change log" file in the round folder that captures,
   per phase:

  - What file was changed (path relative to .claude/skills/singularity/)
  - Type of change (added, modified, removed)
  - One-sentence why (for the receiving session to understand intent)
  - Reference to the synthesis/todo section that drove it

  No line-level diffs, no before/after code. Just enough context that a Claude
  session in the master repo can read our change log, look at our skill folder,
  and understand what's new, what's changed, and what the intent was ‚ÄĒ then
  reconcile from there.

  Want me to create the change log file now and then start Phase 0?

  Proposed structure for the Hard Rules section

  Option A (my recommendation): Two-tier structure within the same Hard Rules 
  section

  Keep the 10 existing rules where they are (they are structural rules about how
   the skill organizes work). Add a new subsection right after them called
  "Behavioral Hard Rules" covering the 15 rules from synthesis ¬ß1 (they are

  Rules so it's loaded as a unit.

  rule for interactive discussion supersedes it. Either add a parenthetical

  rules, which could break references elsewhere in the skill files.
  - Option C: Separate ## Behavioral Rules section. Loses the "read these first,
   all of them" effect of a single Hard Rules section.

  cross-reference to

  the longer rationale.

‚ĚĮ Wait a second, should we have done that, or should we have made a separate    
  rules.md file and added a hook that the skill must read that file before it   
  starts as a mandatory step?                                                   
‚óŹ That's a better design. Two reasons:

  1. SKILL.md is already long. Adding 15 detailed behavioral rules with
  rationale paragraphs makes it substantially longer. Every invocation loads the
   full SKILL.md, so everything in it competes for attention. A separate
  references/hard_rules.md keeps SKILL.md focused on flows and structure while

‚ĚĮ Right after the first check for Singularity happens in the very beginning,    
  the hook should not just be to verify that the file exists, but also to       
  guarantee that Claude actually reads the file. Simply putting a mandatory     
  startup section is good, but that's not enough. It has to be actually

‚óŹ Right. A rule that says "read this file" is just an instruction that can be
  ignored ‚ÄĒ same as the one-question-at-a-time rule lived in memory and was
  ignored. The enforcement has to be deterministic.

  The stop hook can't verify that Claude "read" something in the cognitive
  sense. But it CAN verify that the Read tool was called on that file path
  during the session. The hook receives the conversation data ‚ÄĒ if we check
  whether hard_rules.md was accessed before any write operations happened in an
  engagement folder, that's a real gate.

  However, the stop hook fires at the end (on the Stop event), not at the start.
   For a pre-work gate, we need a different mechanism. Two options:

  Option A: A pre-invocation hook. The skill's frontmatter can define a hook
  that fires when the skill is invoked. That hook could inject a system message
  saying "You MUST read hard_rules.md before proceeding" ‚ÄĒ but that's still
  behavioral, not deterministic.

  Option B: The stop hook checks retroactively. When the stop hook fires, it
  checks: did any engagement files get created or modified during this session?
  If yes, does the conversation history show a Read call to hard_rules.md? If
  engagement work happened without the rules being read, the hook fails with an
  error message telling Claude to read the rules. This means the FIRST time
  Claude tries to do work without reading the rules, it gets caught and has to
  course-correct.

  Option B is the stronger enforcement because it's deterministic and catches
  the violation. The downside is it's retroactive ‚ÄĒ it catches after the first
  piece of work, not before. But that first failure is the teaching moment, and
  from that point the session knows it must read the file.

  Is Option B the right approach, or do you have a different enforcement
  mechanism in mind?

‚óŹ The answer is right there. UserPromptSubmit ‚ÄĒ a hook that fires every time the
   user presses enter, before Claude processes the prompt. It's blocking (YES in
   the Blocking column). It can inject context via stdout that gets fed to
  Claude.

  The pattern:

  1. UserPromptSubmit hook fires on every user message when singularity is
  active
  2. The hook script reads hard_rules.md and outputs its content as stdout
  3. That content gets injected into Claude's context as a system-reminder
  before Claude processes the prompt
  4. Claude literally receives the rules as injected context every single turn ‚ÄĒ
   not "please read this file" but the actual rules text already loaded

  This is Pattern 4 (Context Re-injection) combined with Pattern 9
  (Skill-Scoped). The hook only fires when singularity is active (skill-scoped
  via frontmatter), and it injects the rules content every turn.

  This is far stronger than "read this file" because Claude never has to choose
  to read it ‚ÄĒ the rules arrive automatically as part of the input.

  Want me to implement it this way? The behavioral rules move out of SKILL.md
  into references/hard_rules.md, and a UserPromptSubmit hook in the skill's

‚óŹ Here is my understanding of how hook enforcement works, explained back to you:

  The pattern is: every phase produces artifacts. The stop hook checks that all 
  previous phases' artifacts exist before the current phase is allowed to 
  complete.

  Specifically in django-forge-v2:

  1. Each phase has a defined list of required artifacts (files at specific
  paths, with minimum sizes). These are documented in phase_requirements.md.
  2. The stop hook fires every time Claude finishes a response. It reads the
  state.json to see what phase Claude claims to be in, then walks backward
  through ALL previous phases and checks that every required artifact exists
  with the minimum content size.
  3. If any artifact from a prior phase is missing, the stop hook exits with 
  code 2, which blocks Claude and sends the error message back as feedback.
  Claude cannot proceed without going back and producing the missing artifact.
  4. This means you cannot skip Phase 2 and jump to Phase 3, because the stop
  hook will catch the missing docs_findings.md and block you.
  5. The PreToolUse hook enforces real-time rules (no sed, no arbitrary
  retrieval) by intercepting tool calls before they execute and blocking with
  exit code 2.
  6. The SessionStart hook re-injects context from state.json after compaction
  so the workflow survives context loss.

  Applied to Singularity and hard_rules.md: The enforcement is the same pattern.
   The stop hook should check: before any engagement work artifacts are created,
   was hard_rules.md read? The "proof" that it was read is an artifact ‚ÄĒ either
  a marker file that the mandatory startup step creates after reading, or a
  check in state.json, or simply that the stop hook verifies the file exists and
   the mandatory startup instructions in SKILL.md are gated (like the permission
   check is gated ‚ÄĒ if it fails, the skill stops).

  Now let me add B16 to the open questions document.

‚óŹ Done. Now to your question about stop hooks in settings.json:

  No, the singularity skill currently does NOT check whether its hooks exist in
  the settings.json file or put them in place if missing. The stop hook is
  defined in the skill's SKILL.md frontmatter (the hooks: section at the top),
  which means it fires automatically when the skill is active ‚ÄĒ it does not need
   a separate entry in .claude/settings.json or .claude/settings.local.json.

  However, the permission check (Write and WebSearch) does check
  settings.local.json and offers to add missing permissions. The hooks
  themselves are skill-scoped via frontmatter, so they're automatically active
  when /singularity is invoked and inactive otherwise.

  The question is whether there should be a similar self-check pattern for hooks
   ‚ÄĒ "verify my hooks are properly configured and offer to fix them if not."
  Right now the frontmatter approach handles it implicitly (skill is invoked =
  hooks are active). But if there were hooks that needed to live in
  settings.json instead of frontmatter (for example, hooks that should persist
  across sessions even when the skill is not explicitly invoked), then yes, the
  mandatory startup would need to check for them and install them.

  Is there a specific hook behavior you want to survive beyond the skill
  invocation, or is the frontmatter-scoped approach sufficient for now?

‚úĽ Brewed for 1m 42s

  front matter, then we're okay.

      1 # Nested Singularity (Sub-Singularity) Pattern
      2 
      3 ## What Is a Sub-Singularity
      4 
      5 A sub-singularity is a self-contained singularity instance nested
         within a parent engagement. It has its own source materials, its
         own numbered research chain, its own tracking documents, and its
         own methodology. It follows the same blockchain rules as the par
        ent but with a processing focus tailored to its purpose.
      6 
      7 Sub-singularities are connected to the parent through a **cross-r
        eference file** that maps sub-singularity sets to parent sets whe
        n content overlaps or converges.
      8 
      9 ## When to Create One
     ‚Ä¶ +120 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

      1 # Team Meeting Processing Methodology
      2 
      3 ## Overview
      4 
      5 Team meetings (internal standups, team-to-client syncs, operation
        al check-ins) are processed differently from client discovery mee
        tings. They are operational in nature: focused on action items, b
        lockers, decisions, and progress, not on understanding a client's
         problem or building toward proposals.
      6 
      7 Team meetings are processed within a sub-singularity (see `nested
        _singularity.md`), not in the main engagement research chain.
      8 
      9 ## When This Methodology Applies
     ‚Ä¶ +160 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

      1 # Tracking Folder Pattern
      2 
      3 ## The Dual Model
      4 
      5 Sub-singularities use two complementary persistence mechanisms:
      6 
      7 1. **Research chain (blockchain, immutable).** Per-meeting docume
        nts capture what was said, decided, and discovered at a specific 
        point in time. These are never edited. They are the audit trail.
      8 
      9 2. **Tracking folder (living, editable).** Cumulative operational
         documents that show the current state across all meetings. Updat
        ed after every set is processed. These are the operational dashbo
        ard.

          +chain | Append-only | Yes |                                   
      106 +| `<sub>/tracking/` | Living operational documents (action ite
          +ms, blockers, decisions) | Editable, updated after each set | 
          +Yes (via "Last updated after" header) |                       
      107 +| `<sub>/documents/` | Formatted outputs (HTML reports, status
          + summaries) | Editable | Yes |                                
      108 +| `<sub>/planning/` | Session handoffs, notes for this track |
          + Editable | Yes |                                             
      109 +| `<sub>/cross_reference.md` | Maps sub-singularity sets to pa
          +rent/sibling sets | Editable (living) | N/A |                 
      110 +                                                              
      111 +### Key Distinctions                                          
      112 +                                                              
      113 +- **`deliverables/`** at the engagement root = client-facing d
          +ocuments (multi-page, narrative, sent to client)              
      114 +- **`presentations/`** at the engagement root = slide decks (i
          +ndividual slides for presenting/walking through)              
      115 +- **`planning/`** at the engagement root = internal-only docum
          +ents (meeting summaries for BayOne use, prep notes, session ha
          +ndoffs)                                                       
      116 +- **`documents/`** within a sub-singularity = formatted output
          +s specific to that track (not client-facing deliverables, whic
          +h go in the parent's `deliverables/`)                         
      117 +

      117  4. Each document set covers one source event (a meeting, an em

      121  
      122 +## Application to Sub-Singularities                           
      123 +                                                              
      124 +The blockchain methodology applies identically within each sub
          +-singularity. A sub-singularity has its own research chain wit
          +h its own numbering (01, 02, 03...) independent of the parent.
          + The same immutability rules apply: research documents are nev
          +er edited after creation, summaries are always last, bridge do
          +cuments are retrospective.                                    
      125 +                                                              
      126 +The one addition for sub-singularities is the `tracking/` fold
          +er, which contains living operational documents (action items,
          + blockers, decisions) that ARE editable. These complement the 
          +immutable research chain with a current-state operational view
          +. See `nested_singularity.md` for the full pattern and `tracki
          +ng_folder_pattern.md` for the tracking document specifications
          +.

      10 +## Gold Standard Reference                                     
      11 +                                                               
      12 +Before generating a new presentation, read the gold standard de
         +ck at `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/
         +presentations/srinivas_status/`. The README in that folder expl
         +ains what each slide demonstrates. This is a real engagement de
         +ck that was used in a client meeting and represents the target 
         +quality level.                                                 
      13 +                                                               
      14  ## How to Use This Spec
      15  
      16  This document defines a **design language**, not a rigid templa
          te system. The example layouts below are patterns that have bee
          n proven to work well. When generating presentations:
      17  
      18  1. **Read this spec** for the shared foundation (palette, typog
          raphy, components, rules).
      19  2. **Read the example HTML files** in `.claude/skills/singulari
          ty/assets/slide_examples/` to see how the design language is ap
          plied in practice.
      16 -3. **Design slides that fit the content.** Use example layouts 
         -as inspiration, combine elements from different examples, or cr
         -eate new arrangements that follow the design language. The cont
         -ent determines the layout, not the other way around.           
      20 +3. **Read the gold standard deck** at `assets/design/gold_stand
         +ards/presentations/srinivas_status/` to see the design language
         + applied end-to-end in a real deck.                            
      21 +4. **Design slides that fit the content.** Use example layouts 
         +as inspiration, combine elements from different examples, or cr
         +eate new arrangements that follow the design language. The cont
         +ent determines the layout, not the other way around.           
      22  
      23  The examples are a vocabulary, not a grammar. A well-designed s
          lide that does not match any example exactly but follows the de
          sign language is better than content forced into an ill-fitting
           example layout.

‚óŹ Update(.claude/skills/singularity/references/presentation_design_language.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 47 lines
      227  
      228  **Reference implementation:** See `talent_ai/knowledge_transfe
           r/sessions/session_0/` for the pattern in a long-form document
            context.
      229  
      230 +### Bullet Item Pattern (Default for All Card Bodies)         
      231 +                                                              
      232 +**This is the default content format for all cards.** Paragrap
          +h text in card bodies is a failure mode. Use bullet items inst
          +ead.                                                          
      233 +                                                              
      234 +```html                                                       
      235 +<div class="items">                                           
      236 +  <div class="item"><i class="fa-solid fa-circle"></i><span><s
          +trong>Bold lead phrase</strong> elaboration and detail text</s
          +pan></div>                                                    
      237 +  <div class="item"><i class="fa-solid fa-circle"></i><span><s
          +trong>Another lead</strong> with its description</span></div> 
      238 +</div>                                                        
      239 +```                                                           
      240 +                                                              
      241 +```css                                                        
      242 +.items { display: flex; flex-direction: column; gap: 5px; flex
          +: 1; }                                                        
      243 +.item { display: flex; align-items: flex-start; gap: 8px; font
          +-size: 11px; color: var(--text-light); line-height: 1.45; }   
      244 +.item i { font-size: 5px; color: var(--blue-accent); margin-to
          +p: 5px; flex-shrink: 0; }                                     
      245 +.item strong { color: var(--primary); font-weight: 600; }     
      246 +```                                                           
      247 +                                                              
      248 +**Pattern:** Bold lead phrase sets the key fact. Description t
          +ext after the bold elaborates. Each item is scannable independ
          +ently. 4-6 items per card is the sweet spot.                  
      249 +                                                              
      250 +**When paragraph text IS acceptable:** Short lead paragraphs b
          +elow a slide title (1-2 sentences), takeaway bar content, conn
          +ection strip content. These are framing elements, not card bod
          +ies.                                                          
      251 +                                                              
      252 +### Slide Navigation (Mandatory on All Multi-Slide Decks)     
      253 +                                                              
      254 +Every slide in a multi-slide deck must include prev/next/home 
          +navigation at the bottom-left.                                
      255 +                                                              
      256 +```html                                                       
      257 +<div class="slide-nav">                                       
      258 +  <a href="prev_slide.html"><i class="fa-solid fa-chevron-left
          +"></i></a>                                                    
      259 +  <a href="next_slide.html"><i class="fa-solid fa-chevron-righ
          +t"></i></a>                                                   
      260 +  <a href="00_title.html" style="margin-left: 6px;"><i class="
          +fa-solid fa-house"></i></a>                                   
      261 +</div>                                                        
      262 +```                                                           
      263 +                                                              
      264 +```css                                                        
      265 +.slide-nav { position: fixed; bottom: 18px; left: 18px; displa
          +y: flex; gap: 6px; z-index: 100; }                            
      266 +.slide-nav a { display: flex; align-items: center; justify-con
          +tent: center; width: 36px; height: 36px; border-radius: 8px; b
          +ackground: rgba(12,25,41,0.75); color: rgba(255,255,255,0.7); 
          +text-decoration: none; font-size: 14px; transition: background
          + 0.2s, color 0.2s; border: 1px solid rgba(255,255,255,0.1); cu
          +rsor: pointer; }                                              
      267 +.slide-nav a:hover { background: rgba(37,99,235,0.9); color: #
          +fff; }                                                        
      268 +.slide-nav a.disabled { opacity: 0.25; pointer-events: none; }
      269 +```                                                           
      270 +                                                              
      271 +**Link chain rules:**                                         
      272 +- First slide: prev is `class="disabled"` (no href)           
      273 +- Last slide: next is `class="disabled"` (no href)            
      274 +- Home: always points to `00_title.html`                      
      275 +- Every other slide: prev and next link to adjacent slides in 
          +sequence

‚óŹ Update(.claude/skills/singularity/references/presentation_design_language.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 19 lines
      321  **Examples:** `example_agenda.html`
      322  **Good for:** Table of contents, roadmap, multi-track overview
      323  
      324 +### Dedicated Diagram Slide                                   
      325 +                                                              
      326 +When a mermaid diagram has 4+ nodes, multiple subgraph cluster
          +s, or detail that cannot compress into a compact inline render
          + within a content slide, give the diagram its own dedicated sl
          +ide.                                                          
      327 +                                                              
      328 +Layout: standard header, centered title + lead text, diagram f
          +illing the content area, "Open full-screen diagram" link, foot
          +er. No cards or bullet content ‚ÄĒ the diagram IS the content.  
      329 +                                                              
      330 +**Gold standard:** `gold_standards/presentations/srinivas_stat
          +us/02a_build_ecosystem_diagram.html`                          
      331 +**Chart file:** `gold_standards/charts/example_ecosystem_diagr
          +am.html`                                                      
      332 +**Good for:** Architecture diagrams, data flow diagrams, ecosy
          +stem overviews, workflow visualizations                       
      333 +                                                              
      334 +**Rule:** Do not embed large diagrams inside content slides. T
          +he content gets crowded and the diagram becomes too small to r
          +ead. A dedicated slide plus a full-screen chart file is always
          + the right choice for complex diagrams.                       
      335 +                                                              
      336 +### Status Grid (Colored Indicators)                          
      337 +                                                              
      338 +Multi-column layout with status indicators using colored icons
          +. Green (fa-check-circle, `#22c55e`) for granted/complete, amb
          +er (fa-clock, `#f59e0b`) for in-progress/pending, blue (fa-cir
          +cle-exclamation, blue-accent) for needs-assistance/action-requ
          +ired.

‚óŹ Update(.claude/skills/singularity/references/presentation_design_language.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 37 lines, removed 4 lines
      344  
      345  ## Rules for Generating Slides
      346  
      347 +### Technical Rules                                           
      348 +                                                              
      349  1. **No images or external media.** Font Awesome icons only. N
           o `<img>` tags.
      350  2. **Self-contained HTML.** Each slide is a complete HTML docu
           ment with inline `<style>`. CDN links for fonts and icons only
           .
      351  3. **BayOne Solutions branding.** Logo reads "BayOne Solutions
           ." Blue palette throughout.
      352  4. **Aspect ratio 16:10.** All slides use `aspect-ratio: 16 / 
           10` on the `.slide` container. Max-width 1100px.
      353  5. **Content must fit without scrolling.** If content overflow
           s, split into multiple slides or reduce text.
      352 -6. **No em dashes.** Consistent with singularity deliverable r
          -ules.                                                         
      353 -7. **Professional tone.** No contractions, no emojis, no collo
          -quialisms.                                                    
      354 -8. **Date or context in header-title.** Every content slide sh
          -ows context in the header.                                    
      355 -9. **Mandatory pre-generation reading.** Before generating any
          - presentation slide, the skill (or its agents) must read this 
          -spec AND at least 3 of the example HTML files from `.claude/sk
          -ills/singularity/assets/slide_examples/` to internalize the de
          -sign language. This is enforced by the stop hook.             
      354 +6. **Date or context in header-title.** Every content slide sh
          +ows context in the header.                                    
      355  
      356 +### Content Rules                                             
      357 +                                                              
      358 +7. **Bullet formatting is the default for all card bodies.** U
          +se the `.items` / `.item` pattern, not paragraph text. Paragra
          +phs are only acceptable for lead text, takeaway bars, and conn
          +ection strips. See the Bullet Item Pattern component above.   
      359 +8. **Navigation is mandatory on every slide in a multi-slide d
          +eck.** First slide has prev disabled, last slide has next disa
          +bled, home always points to 00_title.html. See the Slide Navig
          +ation component above.                                        
      360 +9. **Content must use specific details from the source materia
          +l.** Vague corporate language is a failure mode. If the resear
          +ch library says "300K-500K lines per log file," the slide says
          + that, not "substantial log files."                           
      361 +10. **When a section has 4+ substantive points or status indic
          +ators, give it its own slide.** Do not cram access status, det
          +ailed findings, or multi-item checklists into a slide that als
          +o has other content.                                          
      362 +11. **Error on more slides rather than dense slides.** Density
          + reduces readability. If in doubt, split.                     
      363 +12. **Large diagrams go on their own dedicated slide.** Do not
          + embed within content slides. Use the Dedicated Diagram Slide 
          +pattern.                                                      
      364 +13. **No individual names in slide content.** Presenter credit
          + is allowed only on the title and closing slides. Content slid
          +es reference "the team," "the infrastructure team," etc.      
      365 +14. **No direct quotes from any person.** Paraphrase all infor
          +mation as organizational knowledge.                           
      366 +15. **Diplomatic framing for any issue.** Problems are "alignm
          +ent needed" or "items for discussion," not conflicts or critic
          +isms. Existing work is called "prototypes" or "existing automa
          +tion," not failures.                                          
      367 +16. **Architectural ideas framed as preliminary.** Unless expl
          +icitly confirmed by the client, all architecture is "initial t
          +hinking" or "exploratory," not "the plan."                    
      368 +17. **No em dashes.** Consistent with singularity deliverable 
          +rules. Use commas, periods, or "and."                         
      369 +18. **Professional tone.** No contractions, no emojis, no coll
          +oquialisms.                                                   
      370 +                                                              
      371 +### Process Rules                                             
      372 +                                                              
      373 +19. **Mandatory pre-generation reading.** Before generating an
          +y presentation slide, the skill (or its agents) must read this
          + spec, at least 3 of the example HTML files from `.claude/skil
          +ls/singularity/assets/slide_examples/`, AND the gold standard 
          +deck at `assets/design/gold_standards/presentations/srinivas_s
          +tatus/`. This is enforced by the stop hook.                   
      374 +20. **Propose the slide list before generating.** Describe wha
          +t each slide covers and the layout approach in plain language.
          + Get user approval. Then generate.                            
      375 +21. **If a diagram is needed, propose a chart file in `charts/
          +` and a dedicated diagram slide.** Do not embed diagrams in co
          +ntent slides.                                                 
      376 +                                                              
      377 +### Common Failure Modes                                      
      378 +                                                              
      379 +These are patterns that were produced during the first real de
          +ck generation and had to be corrected. They are listed here so
          + they are not repeated.                                       
      380 +                                                              
      381 +| Failure | What Went Wrong | Correct Approach |              
      382 +|---------|----------------|-----------------|                
      383 +| Paragraph text in cards | Cards had wall-of-text description
          +s | Use bullet items (`.items`/`.item`) in every card |       
      384 +| Missing navigation | Slides had no prev/next/home buttons | 
          +Navigation is mandatory on every slide |                      
      385 +| Vague content | Slides said "existing automation" instead of
          + specific details | Draw from the research library: "Python sc
          +ript extracts subset of errors, passes to LLM" |              
      386 +| Dense slides | 5 topics crammed into one slide | Split: acce
          +ss status gets its own slide, diagram gets its own slide |    
      387 +| Diagram embedded in content slide | Content area shrunk, dia
          +gram too small | Dedicated diagram slide with full-screen link
          + |                                                            
      388 +| Missing back button on chart | Full-screen diagram had no wa
          +y to return | Back button is mandatory on all chart pages |   
      389 +                                                              
      390  ---

      344  
      345 +## Sub-Singularities                                          
      346 +                                                              
      347 +Sub-singularities are self-contained mini-singularities nested
          + within an engagement for parallel tracks that would overwhelm
          + the main research chain. The most common use case is team mee
          +ting processing (internal standups, team-to-counterpart syncs)
          +, but the pattern is general-purpose.                         
      348 +                                                              
      349 +**When to create one:** When the engagement has a distinct tra
          +ck of activity with its own source materials, own timeline, an
          +d content that is supplementary to (not part of) the main enga
          +gement narrative. See `references/nested_singularity.md` for t
          +he full pattern, rules, and folder template.                  
      350 +                                                              
      351 +**When invoked:**                                             
      352 +1. Load `references/nested_singularity.md` for the pattern and
          + rules                                                        
      353 +2. If processing a team meeting, also load `references/team_me
          +eting_processing.md` for the standard passes                  
      354 +3. If the sub-singularity has a `tracking/` folder, also load 
          +`references/tracking_folder_pattern.md` for update rules      
      355 +                                                              
      356 +**Key rules:**                                                
      357 +- Each sub-singularity has its own independent numbering chain
          + (01, 02, 03...)                                              
      358 +- The parent's `org_chart.md` is the single people reference (
          +update it from sub-singularity people files)                  
      359 +- The `tracking/` folder is always created (living documents: 
          +action_items.md, blockers.md, decisions.md)                   
      360 +- The `cross_reference.md` file maps sub-singularity sets to p
          +arent sets when content overlaps                              
      361 +- One level of nesting only (no sub-sub-singularities)        
      362 +                                                              
      363 +**Worked example:** `references/worked_example_team/`         
      364 +                                                              
      365 +---

‚úĽ Cogitated for 4m 9s

‚ĚĮ This looks great. The only problem is that the icons are not actually         
  showing. They just say things like fa:fa-check-circle                         

‚óŹ That's likely because mermaid v10 doesn't render the fa: icon syntax the same
  way when htmlLabels: false is set. The icons need htmlLabels: true to render
  as actual Font Awesome glyphs, but we set it to false for the SVG text mode
  that gives us the markdown bold formatting.

  There's a conflict: htmlLabels: false gives us the nice **bold** markdown
  syntax in nodes, but breaks icon rendering. htmlLabels: true renders icons but
   breaks the markdown formatting.

  Let me check which approach v4 used and fix it.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Confirmed ‚ÄĒ htmlLabels: false is the problem. The fa: icon syntax requires
  htmlLabels: true. But we also need the markdown bold formatting which uses the
   "`**text**`" syntax.

  The fix: switch to htmlLabels: true, and replace the markdown bold syntax with
   plain text (since HTML labels don't support the markdown backtick syntax, but
   they DO render FontAwesome icons). For bold, we can use the node label
  structure itself ‚ÄĒ the icon + title on the first line is visually distinct
  enough.

  Let me fix v4 and also create a v4b that tries a different approach using HTML
   <b> tags if mermaid supports them with htmlLabels.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Key finding: the fa: syntax works with standard square-bracket labels and
  htmlLabels: true (or default). The issue is mixing it with the markdown
  backtick syntax which requires htmlLabels: false.

  The solution: switch to htmlLabels: true, drop the markdown backtick
  formatting, and use plain fa:fa-icon Title\nDescription format. The icons will
   render as actual glyphs.

  markdown bold formatting requires htmlLabels: false, but icon rendering
  requires htmlLabels: true. They're mutually exclusive in mermaid v10. If the

   get both ‚ÄĒ which is a separate upgrade path. Open the file and let me know

‚óŹ Good. The approach for v11: upgrade the CDN to mermaid v11, register
  FontAwesome as an icon pack, then we can use BOTH the @{icon:} shapes (which
  render real icons) AND keep the markdown bold syntax in regular nodes. But the
   @{icon:} nodes are a different shape type ‚ÄĒ they show an icon with a label,
  not a box with multi-line text.

  The better v11 approach might be: keep the regular node shapes with markdown
  bold text (which works with htmlLabels: false), AND separately place icon
  nodes as visual decorators. But that's complex.

  The simplest approach: upgrade to mermaid v11, switch to htmlLabels: true
  which in v11 should support BOTH FA icons and basic HTML formatting (<b> tags
  instead of markdown **). Let me make a v5 that tries the v11 upgrade path
  while preserving the v3 layout.

‚óŹ Try it now. This approach waits until after mermaid renders the SVG, then
  finds each cluster label element and inserts a white rectangle behind the text
   within the SVG itself. The rect sits in the same SVG group as the label, so
  it should layer correctly ‚ÄĒ text on top of the white rect, both on top of the
  arrows passing beneath.

‚ĚĮ Claude, the arrows are still over top. What's going on here? Why did this     
  work, for instance, for those small things with the blue background that are  
  commits and commits plus PRs? How do those work? Answer back. Stop messing    
  around with the code because we're just spinning wheels right now. The white  
  border is showing now, and it is showing vertically on top of the blue box,   
  which is good, but the arrow is still overlapping.                            

‚óŹ The issue is SVG rendering order. SVG has no z-index ‚ÄĒ elements paint in
  document order, top to bottom in the DOM. Later elements paint on top of
  earlier ones.

  Here's why the edge labels ("Commits", "Log Output") work: mermaid renders
  them AFTER the arrows in the SVG. So the paint order is arrows first, then
  edge labels on top. The opaque edgeLabelBackground rect sits on top of the
  arrow line because it comes later in the DOM.

  The cluster titles ("DATA STORAGE") DON'T work because mermaid renders the
  entire cluster group (background + title) BEFORE the edges. The SVG DOM order
  is:

  1. Cluster groups (background rects + title labels) ‚ÄĒ painted first
  2. Node groups ‚ÄĒ painted second
  3. Edge groups (arrows + edge labels) ‚ÄĒ painted last, on top of everything

  My white rect is inside the cluster group, so it's still underneath the edges
  no matter what I do within that group. The arrows paint OVER the entire
  cluster group because they come later in the SVG document.

  The fix: after mermaid renders, use JavaScript to MOVE the cluster label
  elements to the end of the SVG so they render last ‚ÄĒ on top of the arrows,
  just like edge labels do. Want me to try that approach?

‚ĚĮ Go ahead and try it.

‚óŹ Try it now. The approach: after mermaid renders, for each cluster label I
  clone it into a new SVG group with a white background rect, append that group
  to the very end of the SVG (so it paints last, on top of everything including
  arrows), then hide the original label to prevent double-rendering.

‚óŹ The script now finds the parent cluster's <rect> element, grabs its stroke
  color, and applies that as the border on the label background. So the blue box
   titles get a blue border, yellow get yellow, red get red, green get green.
